        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        <p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>





When creating a date time chooser on Android, a Java object named DateTimeChooserAndroid is created which takes a raw pointer nativeDateTimeChooserAndroid and stores it as a member [1]. When user clicks the 'set' button on date time dialog, replaceDateTime will be called and then use the native pointer for JNI function call [2]. However, a UAF would occur if the c++ object DateTimeChooserAndroid that the raw pointer refers to has been freed at that time. This can be done by simply closing the web page because DateTimeChooserAndroid is attached to the specified WebContents.



<span class="line"><!---->When creating a date time chooser on Android, a Java object named DateTimeChooserAndroid is created which takes a raw pointer nativeDateTimeChooserAndroid and stores it as a member [1]. When user clicks the 'set' button on date time dialog, replaceDateTime will be called and then use the native pointer for JNI function call [2]. However, a UAF would occur if the c++ object DateTimeChooserAndroid that the raw pointer refers to has been freed at that time. This can be done by simply closing the web page because DateTimeChooserAndroid is attached to the specified WebContents.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>





private DateTimeChooserAndroid(Context context,



<span class="line"><!---->private DateTimeChooserAndroid(Context context,<!----></span>



<br>





        long nativeDateTimeChooserAndroid) {



<span class="line"><!---->        long nativeDateTimeChooserAndroid) {<!----></span>



<br>





    mNativeDateTimeChooserAndroid = nativeDateTimeChooserAndroid;  // ===> [1]



<span class="line"><!---->    mNativeDateTimeChooserAndroid = nativeDateTimeChooserAndroid;  // ===&gt; [1]<!----></span>



<br>





    mInputDialogContainer = new InputDialogContainer(context,



<span class="line"><!---->    mInputDialogContainer = new InputDialogContainer(context,<!----></span>



<br>





            new InputDialogContainer.InputActionDelegate() {



<span class="line"><!---->            new InputDialogContainer.InputActionDelegate() {<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





                @Override



<span class="line"><!---->                @Override<!----></span>



<br>





                public void replaceDateTime(double value) {        // ===> [2]



<span class="line"><!---->                public void replaceDateTime(double value) {        // ===&gt; [2]<!----></span>



<br>





                    DateTimeChooserAndroidJni.get().replaceDateTime(



<span class="line"><!---->                    DateTimeChooserAndroidJni.get().replaceDateTime(<!----></span>



<br>





                            mNativeDateTimeChooserAndroid, DateTimeChooserAndroid.this, value);



<span class="line"><!---->                            mNativeDateTimeChooserAndroid, DateTimeChooserAndroid.this, value);<!----></span>



<br>





                }



<span class="line"><!---->                }<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





                @Override



<span class="line"><!---->                @Override<!----></span>



<br>





                public void cancelDateTimeDialog() {



<span class="line"><!---->                public void cancelDateTimeDialog() {<!----></span>



<br>





                    DateTimeChooserAndroidJni.get().cancelDialog(



<span class="line"><!---->                    DateTimeChooserAndroidJni.get().cancelDialog(<!----></span>



<br>





                            mNativeDateTimeChooserAndroid, DateTimeChooserAndroid.this);



<span class="line"><!---->                            mNativeDateTimeChooserAndroid, DateTimeChooserAndroid.this);<!----></span>



<br>





                }



<span class="line"><!---->                }<!----></span>



<br>





            });



<span class="line"><!---->            });<!----></span>



<br>





}



<span class="line"><!---->}<!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>

VERSION



<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>



<br>





Chrome Version: 96.0.4664.45 (stable) + dev



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome Version: 96.0.4664.45 (stable) + dev<!----></span>



<br>





Operating System: Android



<span class="line"><!---->Operating System: Android<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





REPRODUCTION CASE



<b class="line"><!---->REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></b>



<br>





1. Setup a local HTTP server



<span class="line"><!---->1. Setup a local HTTP server<!----></span>



<br>





python -m SimpleHTTPServer 8000



<span class="line"><!---->python -m SimpleHTTPServer 8000<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





2. Create a port forwarding from Android device to the local machine



<span class="line"><!---->2. Create a port forwarding from Android device to the local machine<!----></span>



<br>





adb reverse tcp:8000 tcp:8000



<span class="line"><!---->adb reverse tcp:8000 tcp:8000<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





3. Launch chrome on Android and navigate to 



<span class="line"><!---->3. Launch chrome on Android and navigate to <!----></span>





http://localhost:8000/poc.html



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="http://localhost:8000/poc.html"><!---->http://localhost:8000/poc.html<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





4. Click 'Click Me' button on the page



<span class="line"><!---->4. Click 'Click Me' button on the page<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





5. Click the input element to open the date time chooser and click any button on the dialog



<span class="line"><!---->5. Click the input element to open the date time chooser and click any button on the dialog<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





Note 



<span class="line"><!---->Note <!----></span>



<br>





1. UAF happens in the browser process and can be triggered WITHOUT compromised render. 



<span class="line"><!---->1. UAF happens in the browser process and can be triggered WITHOUT compromised render. <!----></span>



<br>





2. The poc requires several click, but only one click on the chooser dialog is really needed if the renderer is already compromised.



<span class="line"><!---->2. The poc requires several click, but only one click on the chooser dialog is really needed if the renderer is already compromised.<!----></span>

It might take longer for me to have the fix. Because the root cause is not just because the DateTimeChooserAndroid Java object didn't clear the native pointer and didn't dismiss. More seriously, it is because we didn't implement the logic to close the popup window if Blink think it is the time to dismiss the popup. When navigating away from the current web page, Blink will actually issue a signal to dismiss the popup, but we didn't wire the signal to browser process.



<span class="line"><!---->It might take longer for me to have the fix. Because the root cause is not just because the DateTimeChooserAndroid Java object didn't clear the native pointer and didn't dismiss. More seriously, it is because we didn't implement the logic to close the popup window if Blink think it is the time to dismiss the popup. When navigating away from the current web page, Blink will actually issue a signal to dismiss the popup, but we didn't wire the signal to browser process.<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->commit <!----></span>





9404000e28b0bf7a673cbb174daab050bcf90b50



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://crrev.com/9404000e28b0bf7a673cbb174daab050bcf90b50"><!---->9404000e28b0bf7a673cbb174daab050bcf90b50<!----></a>

Author: Shimi Zhang <



<span class="line"><!---->Author: Shimi Zhang &lt;<!----></span>

<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="/u/ctzsm@chromium.org"><!---->ctzsm@chromium.org<!----></a>

<br>





Date: Tue Dec 14 18:10:36 2021



<span class="line"><!---->Date: Tue Dec 14 18:10:36 2021<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[Android] Send dismissal signal from Blink to browser for DateTimeChooser



<span class="line"><!---->[Android] Send dismissal signal from Blink to browser for DateTimeChooser<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





On Android, the DateTimeChooser is a browser side Android native popup



<span class="line"><!---->On Android, the DateTimeChooser is a browser side Android native popup<!----></span>



<br>





window, which is an external DateTimeChooser from Blink's perspective.



<span class="line"><!---->window, which is an external DateTimeChooser from Blink's perspective.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





When Blink wants to dismiss the DateTimePicker, it will send a



<span class="line"><!---->When Blink wants to dismiss the DateTimePicker, it will send a<!----></span>



<br>





EndChooser() signal. Previously, we didn't wire this signal to browser



<span class="line"><!---->EndChooser() signal. Previously, we didn't wire this signal to browser<!----></span>



<br>





process for Android, therefore, when blink wants to dismiss the



<span class="line"><!---->process for Android, therefore, when blink wants to dismiss the<!----></span>



<br>





popup window, e.g. before navigating away from the current URL, the



<span class="line"><!---->popup window, e.g. before navigating away from the current URL, the<!----></span>



<br>





popup window will still remain there.



<span class="line"><!---->popup window will still remain there.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





We also guard the Java DateTimeChooser to use the native pointer when



<span class="line"><!---->We also guard the Java DateTimeChooser to use the native pointer when<!----></span>



<br>





the corresponding native object is gone.



<span class="line"><!---->the corresponding native object is gone.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

[Android] Send dismissal signal from Blink to browser for DateTimeChooser



<span class="line"><!---->[Android] Send dismissal signal from Blink to browser for DateTimeChooser<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





On Android, the DateTimeChooser is a browser side Android native popup



<span class="line"><!---->On Android, the DateTimeChooser is a browser side Android native popup<!----></span>



<br>





window, which is an external DateTimeChooser from Blink's perspective.



<span class="line"><!---->window, which is an external DateTimeChooser from Blink's perspective.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





When Blink wants to dismiss the DateTimePicker, it will send a



<span class="line"><!---->When Blink wants to dismiss the DateTimePicker, it will send a<!----></span>



<br>





EndChooser() signal. Previously, we didn't wire this signal to browser



<span class="line"><!---->EndChooser() signal. Previously, we didn't wire this signal to browser<!----></span>



<br>





process for Android, therefore, when blink wants to dismiss the



<span class="line"><!---->process for Android, therefore, when blink wants to dismiss the<!----></span>



<br>





popup window, e.g. before navigating away from the current URL, the



<span class="line"><!---->popup window, e.g. before navigating away from the current URL, the<!----></span>



<br>





popup window will still remain there.



<span class="line"><!---->popup window will still remain there.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





We also guard the Java DateTimeChooser to use the native pointer when



<span class="line"><!---->We also guard the Java DateTimeChooser to use the native pointer when<!----></span>



<br>





the corresponding native object is gone.



<span class="line"><!---->the corresponding native object is gone.<!----></span>

On Android, the DateTimeChooser is a browser side Android native popup



<span class="line"><!---->On Android, the DateTimeChooser is a browser side Android native popup<!----></span>



<br>





window, which is an external DateTimeChooser from Blink's perspective.



<span class="line"><!---->window, which is an external DateTimeChooser from Blink's perspective.<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->When Blink wants to dismiss the DateTimePicker, it will send a<!----></span>



<br>





EndChooser() signal. Previously, we didn't wire this signal to browser



<span class="line"><!---->EndChooser() signal. Previously, we didn't wire this signal to browser<!----></span>



<br>





process for Android, therefore, when blink wants to dismiss the



<span class="line"><!---->process for Android, therefore, when blink wants to dismiss the<!----></span>



<br>





popup window, e.g. before navigating away from the current URL, the



<span class="line"><!---->popup window, e.g. before navigating away from the current URL, the<!----></span>



<br>





popup window will still remain there.



<span class="line"><!---->popup window will still remain there.<!----></span>

[Android] Send dismissal signal from Blink to browser for DateTimeChooser



<span class="line"><!---->[Android] Send dismissal signal from Blink to browser for DateTimeChooser<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





On Android, the DateTimeChooser is a browser side Android native popup



<span class="line"><!---->On Android, the DateTimeChooser is a browser side Android native popup<!----></span>



<br>





window, which is an external DateTimeChooser from Blink's perspective.



<span class="line"><!---->window, which is an external DateTimeChooser from Blink's perspective.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





When Blink wants to dismiss the DateTimePicker, it will send a



<span class="line"><!---->When Blink wants to dismiss the DateTimePicker, it will send a<!----></span>



<br>





EndChooser() signal. Previously, we didn't wire this signal to browser



<span class="line"><!---->EndChooser() signal. Previously, we didn't wire this signal to browser<!----></span>



<br>





process for Android, therefore, when blink wants to dismiss the



<span class="line"><!---->process for Android, therefore, when blink wants to dismiss the<!----></span>



<br>





popup window, e.g. before navigating away from the current URL, the



<span class="line"><!---->popup window, e.g. before navigating away from the current URL, the<!----></span>



<br>





popup window will still remain there.



<span class="line"><!---->popup window will still remain there.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





We also guard the Java DateTimeChooser to use the native pointer when



<span class="line"><!---->We also guard the Java DateTimeChooser to use the native pointer when<!----></span>



<br>





the corresponding native object is gone.



<span class="line"><!---->the corresponding native object is gone.<!----></span>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.
